{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01KbLodi1TThjcGuyecuPnCN","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01YbxpWACUGVUFLnVzghn1V1","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide\n## From Version 1.30.0 to Version 1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## Overview\n\nThis guide documents the changes to the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter between versions 1.30.0 (April 2024) and 1.31.0 (July 2024). The ext_proc filter allows external gRPC services to process HTTP requests and responses in a flexible and powerful way.\n\nThe 1.31.0 release introduces improvements to route cache handling, observability mode enhancements, and changes to the immediate response message format. Most applications will continue to work without changes, but some configuration updates may be beneficial for optimal performance and to take advantage of new features.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. ImmediateResponse.body Field Type Change (Critical)\n\n**Impact:** Applications using the `ImmediateResponse` message to send immediate responses with body content.\n\n**What Changed:**\nThe `body` field in the `ImmediateResponse` message has been changed from `string` to `bytes`.\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;  // <-- was string\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;  // <-- changed to bytes\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**Why This Changed:**\nChanging to `bytes` allows more flexible handling of binary content and is more idiomatic for protobuf. The `string` type in protobuf enforces UTF-8 validation, which can be restrictive for response bodies that may contain binary data or non-UTF-8 encoded content.\n\n**Migration Action Required:**\n- **For Go clients:** Code must change from `response.GetBody()` (returns `string`) to `response.GetBody()` (returns `[]byte`). Generated code will handle this automatically with regenerated protobuf files.\n- **For Python clients:** Code using `response.body` will now return `bytes` instead of `str`. String responses should be encoded: `response.body = your_string.encode('utf-8')`\n- **For other languages:** Regenerate protobuf code and update type conversions accordingly.\n\n**Example:**\n\nGo (before):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   \"Hello World\",  // string\n}\n```\n\nGo (after):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Hello World\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. disable_clear_route_cache Field (Deprecated with Replacement)\n\n**Deprecation Status:** Marked for future removal (recommended to migrate)\n\n**What's Happening:**\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is being superseded by a new `route_cache_action` enum that provides more granular control over route cache behavior.\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ... other fields ...\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // Default: clear route cache when external processor response sets\n    // clear_route_cache = true\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear route cache regardless of clear_route_cache field\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Never clear route cache regardless of clear_route_cache field\n    // (equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache = true)\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  // ... other fields ...\n\n  // Deprecated: use route_cache_action instead\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Recommended: new field for route cache control\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Recommendation:**\n\n| Old Configuration | New Configuration | Behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Default behavior - respect external processor's clear_route_cache field |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear route cache |\n| Not set | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | (New) Always clear route cache |\n\n**Example:**\n\nYAML (before - v1.30):\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nYAML (after - v1.31, recommended):\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Replaces disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**What It Is:**\nA new enum-based configuration that replaces the boolean `disable_clear_route_cache` flag with more explicit control over route cache behavior in response to external processor requests.\n\n**Field Details:**\n- **Field Number:** 18\n- **Type:** `enum RouteCacheAction`\n- **Location:** `ExternalProcessor` message in `ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Values:**\n\n| Value | Name | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| 0 | DEFAULT | Clear route cache only when the external processor response sets `clear_route_cache = true`. This is the default behavior and maintains backward compatibility. |\n| 1 | CLEAR | Always clear the route cache when processing request headers, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the external processor response. Use this when headers are frequently modified in ways that affect routing. |\n| 2 | RETAIN | Never clear the route cache, even if the external processor response sets `clear_route_cache = true`. Use this when you're confident that header modifications won't affect routing, to improve performance. |\n\n**When to Use Each:**\n\n- **DEFAULT:** Most common use case. Allows the external processor to indicate when the route needs to be recomputed based on header modifications.\n- **CLEAR:** When the external processor frequently modifies routing-critical headers (e.g., authority, path) and you want to ensure the route is always recomputed for safety.\n- **RETAIN:** Performance optimization when headers are modified but routing is known to be unaffected (e.g., only adding custom headers).\n\n**Implementation Note:**\nThe configuration is only applied to request headers processing. The field is ignored for body and trailer responses.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Management\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**What It Is:**\nEnhanced support for observability mode with deferred stream closure management. Previously, gRPC streams would be immediately closed in observability mode. Now they can be held open longer to ensure all data is delivered.\n\n**New Fields:**\n\n**Field: deferred_close_timeout**\n- **Field Number:** 19\n- **Type:** `google.protobuf.Duration`\n- **Default:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n- **Description:** Specifies how long to keep gRPC streams open after the HTTP request/response lifecycle completes when running in observability mode.\n\n**Configuration Example:**\n\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Wait 10 seconds before closing streams\n```\n\n**How It Works:**\n\nIn observability mode:\n1. Envoy sends requests to the external processor without expecting responses\n2. The external processor cannot modify the request/response\n3. With `deferred_close_timeout`, the stream stays open for the specified duration after the HTTP stream ends\n4. This ensures all observability data reaches the external processor reliably\n5. After the timeout, the stream is automatically closed\n\n**Typical Use Cases:**\n- Monitoring and logging services that need to observe all traffic\n- Analytics collection that doesn't require low-latency responses\n- Security monitoring and intrusion detection systems\n\n---\n\n### 3. Enhanced Implementation Infrastructure\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**Behind-the-Scenes Changes:**\n\nTwo new internal classes were added to support deferred stream closure:\n\n1. **ThreadLocalStreamManager:** Manages the lifecycle of gRPC streams with deferred closure support\n   - Stores streams in a thread-local map by stream ID\n   - Handles deferred erasure (closure) of streams\n   - Ensures stream cleanup happens on the correct thread\n\n2. **DeferredDeletableStream:** Wraps a gRPC stream with deferred closure capability\n   - Sets up a timer for deferred closure\n   - Tracks stream lifecycle until the timer fires\n   - Manages resources properly across thread boundaries\n\n**Impact:** These are internal implementation details. Users don't need to interact with them directly, but they enable the observability mode enhancements described above.\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Summary of Configuration Changes\n\n| Aspect | v1.30 | v1.31 | Migration Path |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Route Cache Control | `disable_clear_route_cache` (bool) | `route_cache_action` (enum) + deprecated bool | Migrate to enum |\n| Deferred Close | Not supported | `deferred_close_timeout` | Add if using observability mode |\n| Immediate Response Body | `string` | `bytes` | Update client code |\n| Stream Lifecycle | Immediate close | Deferred close (configurable) | Configure as needed |\n\n### Full Configuration Template (v1.31)\n\n```yaml\n# HTTP Connection Manager configuration\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n\n    # Required: gRPC service configuration\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      timeout: 5s\n\n    # Optional: failure handling\n    failure_mode_allow: false\n\n    # Optional: processing mode (what to send to external processor)\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: NONE\n      response_body_mode: NONE\n      request_trailer_mode: SKIP\n      response_trailer_mode: SKIP\n\n    # Optional: message timeout\n    message_timeout: 200ms\n    max_message_timeout: 10s\n\n    # Optional: statistics prefix\n    stat_prefix: my_ext_proc\n\n    # Optional: header mutation rules\n    mutation_rules:\n      allow_all_routing:\n        value: true\n      allow_envoy:\n        value: true\n\n    # NEW in v1.31: route cache control\n    # RECOMMENDED: use route_cache_action instead of disable_clear_route_cache\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # or CLEAR, or RETAIN\n\n    # DEPRECATED in v1.31: use route_cache_action instead\n    # disable_clear_route_cache: false\n\n    # Optional: allow mode override\n    allow_mode_override: true\n\n    # Optional: disable immediate response\n    disable_immediate_response: false\n\n    # Optional: header forwarding rules\n    forward_rules:\n      allowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - exact: \"custom-header\"\n      disallowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - prefix: \"secret-\"\n\n    # Optional: dynamic metadata options\n    metadata_options:\n      forwarding_namespaces:\n        untyped:\n        - my_namespace\n      receiving_namespaces:\n        untyped:\n        - response_namespace\n\n    # Optional: observability mode\n    observability_mode: true\n\n    # NEW in v1.31: deferred close timeout for observability mode\n    deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Default is 5000ms\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Handling\n\n**Default Behavior Change (Minor):**\n\nIn v1.30, `disable_clear_route_cache` defaulted to `false`, which meant:\n- Clear route cache when external processor sets `clear_route_cache = true`\n- Keep route cache otherwise\n\nIn v1.31, `route_cache_action` defaults to `DEFAULT`, which has the same behavior:\n- Clear route cache when external processor sets `clear_route_cache = true`\n- Keep route cache otherwise\n\n**Impact:** If you're using the defaults, there's no behavior change.\n\n**If you had `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n- Old behavior: Never clear route cache\n- New equivalent: `route_cache_action: RETAIN` (same behavior)\n- Recommendation: Update configuration to use the new enum\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Handling\n\n**New Behavior:**\n\nStreams in observability mode are now managed with deferred closure:\n\n1. Stream stays open for `deferred_close_timeout` after HTTP stream completes\n2. Allows all pending observability messages to reach the external processor\n3. Stream is then automatically closed\n\n**Old Behavior (v1.30):**\nStreams were closed as soon as the HTTP request/response processing completed.\n\n**Impact:**\n\n- **Improved Reliability:** Observability data is less likely to be lost\n- **Slight Resource Usage:** Streams hold resources for up to 5 seconds (default) after completion\n- **Configurable:** Adjust `deferred_close_timeout` based on your external processor's processing speed\n\n**Example Scenario:**\n\nExternal processor doing log aggregation in observability mode:\n- Request completes in 100ms\n- Stream would close immediately (v1.30) or after 5s (v1.31, default)\n- Asyncronous logging operations in the external processor have more time to complete\n- Logs are more likely to be captured and forwarded before stream closure\n\n### 3. Immediate Response Format Compatibility\n\n**Technical Impact:**\n\nThe `body` field type change from `string` to `bytes` in `ImmediateResponse` requires regenerating protobuf files in external processors.\n\n**Runtime Behavior:**\n- If the external processor doesn't send body content, no changes needed\n- If body content is sent as UTF-8 text, automatic encoding/decoding handles it\n- If body content contains binary data, the new `bytes` type is actually more appropriate\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n\nReview your ext_proc filter configurations to identify:\n\n1. **Do you use `disable_clear_route_cache`?**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/config\n   ```\n   - If yes, go to Step 2\n   - If no, skip to Step 3\n\n2. **Do you use observability mode?**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"observability_mode.*true\" /path/to/config\n   ```\n   - If yes, go to Step 3\n   - If no, skip to Step 4\n\n### Step 2: Migrate disable_clear_route_cache\n\nUpdate each configuration that uses `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**Find:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Replace with:**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Or find:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: false\n# or not set (defaults to false)\n```\n\n**Replace with:**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n### Step 3: Configure Deferred Close Timeout (Optional)\n\nIf using observability mode, consider adding explicit configuration:\n\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Adjust based on your external processor\n```\n\nThe default is 5 seconds. Adjust based on:\n- How fast your external processor can process messages\n- How much resource overhead you can tolerate\n- How critical it is to deliver all observability data\n\n**Recommendations:**\n- **1-2 seconds:** For high-throughput scenarios with fast processors\n- **5 seconds (default):** Balanced approach for most use cases\n- **10+ seconds:** For slow processors or when observability is critical\n\n### Step 4: Update External Processor Code\n\nIf your external processor sends `ImmediateResponse` messages:\n\n**Python Example:**\n\nBefore (v1.30):\n```python\nfrom envoy.service.ext_proc.v3 import external_processor_pb2\n\nresponse = external_processor_pb2.ImmediateResponse()\nresponse.status.code = 200\nresponse.body = \"Hello World\"  # string\n```\n\nAfter (v1.31):\n```python\nfrom envoy.service.ext_proc.v3 import external_processor_pb2\n\nresponse = external_processor_pb2.ImmediateResponse()\nresponse.status.code = 200\nresponse.body = b\"Hello World\"  # bytes\n```\n\n**Go Example:**\n\nBefore (v1.30):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   \"Hello World\",  // string\n}\n```\n\nAfter (v1.31):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Hello World\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n**Regenerate Protobuf Bindings:**\n\nAll language bindings need to be regenerated with the updated protobuf definitions:\n\n```bash\n# Go\nprotoc --go_out=. envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto\n\n# Python\npython -m grpc_tools.protoc ...\n\n# Node.js\ngrpc_tools_node_protoc ...\n\n# See language-specific documentation for exact commands\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test and Validate\n\n#### Configuration Validation\n\n```bash\n# Check syntax\nenvoy -c your-config.yaml --mode validate_only\n\n# Verify ext_proc filter is loaded\nenvoy -c your-config.yaml --mode dump_config | grep ext_proc\n```\n\n#### Functional Testing\n\n1. **Test with observability mode disabled:**\n   - Verify normal request processing works\n   - Confirm route cache behavior matches expectations\n   - Check metrics and logs\n\n2. **Test with observability mode enabled:**\n   - Send traffic through the filter\n   - Verify all observability messages reach the external processor\n   - Monitor for lost data with and without `deferred_close_timeout`\n   - Check CPU and memory impact\n\n3. **Test ImmediateResponse (if applicable):**\n   - Send immediate responses from external processor\n   - Verify body content is correctly delivered to client\n   - Test with binary response data if applicable\n\n#### Metrics to Monitor\n\n```\n# Route cache metrics\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.clear_route_cache_ignored\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.clear_route_cache_disabled\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.clear_route_cache_upstream_ignored\n\n# Stream metrics\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.streams_started\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.streams_closed\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.streams_failed\n```\n\n### Step 6: Canary Deployment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy binary to a canary environment\n2. Route 5-10% of traffic to canary instances\n3. Monitor for 24-48 hours:\n   - Error rates\n   - Latency percentiles\n   - External processor CPU/memory usage\n   - Observability data completeness\n4. If issues arise, adjust `deferred_close_timeout` or `route_cache_action` settings\n5. Gradually increase traffic percentage\n6. Full production rollout\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Unit Test Updates\n\nFor external processor implementations, update unit tests:\n\n**Python:**\n```python\ndef test_immediate_response_body():\n    # v1.31 requires bytes, not string\n    response = external_processor_pb2.ImmediateResponse()\n    response.body = b\"test content\"\n    assert isinstance(response.body, bytes)\n    assert response.body == b\"test content\"\n```\n\n**Go:**\n```go\nfunc TestImmediateResponseBody(t *testing.T) {\n    resp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n        Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n        Body:   []byte(\"test content\"),\n    }\n    assert.Equal(t, []byte(\"test content\"), resp.GetBody())\n}\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n1. **Route Cache Control:**\n   - Test with `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` - verify external processor can trigger cache clear\n   - Test with `route_cache_action: CLEAR` - verify cache always clears\n   - Test with `route_cache_action: RETAIN` - verify cache never clears\n\n2. **Observability Mode:**\n   - Enable observability mode with various `deferred_close_timeout` values\n   - Send requests that modify headers\n   - Verify all observability messages reach the external processor\n   - Measure stream lifecycle and resource usage\n\n3. **Immediate Response:**\n   - Send immediate responses with text body\n   - Send immediate responses with binary body\n   - Verify content reaches client correctly\n\n### Performance Testing\n\n```bash\n# Load test with observability mode on/off\n# Monitor:\n# - CPU usage\n# - Memory usage\n# - Stream open/close rates\n# - Lost observability messages\n# - Latency impact\n\nwrk -t 4 -c 100 -d 60s \\\n    -s /path/to/script.lua \\\n    http://envoy:8080/test_path\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Issues Occur After Upgrade\n\n1. **Immediate Action:**\n   ```bash\n   # Roll back to v1.30\n   systemctl stop envoy\n   cp /path/to/envoy-v1.30 /usr/local/bin/envoy\n   systemctl start envoy\n   ```\n\n2. **Before Next Upgrade Attempt:**\n   - Identify the problematic feature (route cache, observability, immediate response)\n   - Disable or adjust that feature\n   - Run targeted tests\n   - Attempt upgrade again\n\n3. **Common Rollback Scenarios:**\n\n   **Scenario: External processor crashes on receiving ImmediateResponse**\n   - Cause: Protobuf mismatch on body field (bytes vs string)\n   - Solution: Regenerate protobuf bindings in external processor\n   - Prevention: Test with external processor built against v1.31 protobuf definitions\n\n   **Scenario: Route cache behavior changed unexpectedly**\n   - Cause: Didn't update `disable_clear_route_cache` to new enum\n   - Solution: Explicitly set `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (same as old default)\n   - Prevention: Review configuration and test route behavior\n\n   **Scenario: High resource usage with observability mode**\n   - Cause: Default 5-second deferred close timeout too long for your workload\n   - Solution: Reduce `deferred_close_timeout` to 1-2 seconds\n   - Prevention: Test and tune timeout value before full rollout\n\n---\n\n## Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Mixing Old and New Configuration Styles\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting settings!\n```\n\n**Solution:** Use only `route_cache_action`. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache`.\n\n### Pitfall 2: Not Regenerating Protobuf Code\n\n**Problem:** External processor fails when receiving `ImmediateResponse` from v1.31 Envoy.\n\n**Cause:** Old protobuf code expects `body` to be string, but v1.31 Envoy sends bytes.\n\n**Solution:**\n```bash\n# Regenerate all protobuf bindings\npython -m grpc_tools.protoc \\\n    --python_out=. \\\n    --grpc_python_out=. \\\n    -I/path/to/envoy/api \\\n    -I/path/to/googleapis \\\n    envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Observability Data Loss with Short Timeout\n\n**Problem:** In observability mode with short `deferred_close_timeout`, async logging operations in external processor don't complete before stream closes.\n\n**Solution:** Increase `deferred_close_timeout` based on external processor's typical processing time:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Increase from default 5s\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Not Testing Route Cache Behavior\n\n**Problem:** After upgrade, routing behavior changes unexpectedly.\n\n**Cause:** Didn't explicitly set `route_cache_action`, relying on undefined default behavior.\n\n**Solution:** Always explicitly set the value:\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Be explicit about intended behavior\n```\n\n### Pitfall 5: Canary Test with Old External Processor Version\n\n**Problem:** Canary deployment with v1.31 Envoy but v1.30 external processor fails.\n\n**Cause:** ImmediateResponse body format mismatch.\n\n**Solution:** Upgrade external processor to v1.31 compatible version first, or thoroughly test compatibility.\n\n---\n\n## Backwards Compatibility Notes\n\n### What's Backwards Compatible\n\n- ✅ Normal request/response processing\n- ✅ Default configurations (will work with v1.30 external processors)\n- ✅ Processing modes and timeout configuration\n- ✅ Header mutation rules\n\n### What Requires Updates\n\n- ❌ `ImmediateResponse.body` field (type change: string → bytes)\n- ❌ `disable_clear_route_cache` (replacement with `route_cache_action` enum)\n- ❌ Observability mode with deferred closure (v1.31 feature)\n\n### Migration Strategy for Large Deployments\n\n1. **Phase 1:** Deploy v1.31 Envoy with all old configurations (will work)\n2. **Phase 2:** Update external processor code to handle bytes body\n3. **Phase 3:** Update Envoy configurations to use new enums\n4. **Phase 4:** Optimize observability mode settings\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Official Documentation\n\n- [Envoy External Processing Filter Documentation](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter)\n- [ext_proc Proto API Forum](https://discuss.envoyproxy.io/)\n- [Slack Community](https://envoyproxy.slack.com/)\n\n---\n\n## Checklist for Successful Migration\n\n- [ ] Review current ext_proc configurations\n- [ ] The ext_proc filter allows external gRPC services to process HTTP requests and responses in a flexible and powerful way.\n\nThe 1.31.0 release introduces improvements to route cache handling, observability mode enhancements, and changes to the immediate response message format. Most applications will continue to work without changes, but some configuration updates may be beneficial for optimal performance and to take advantage of new features.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. ImmediateResponse.body Field Type Change (Critical)\n\n**Impact:** Applications using the `ImmediateResponse` message to send immediate responses with body content.\n\n**What Changed:**\nThe `body` field in the `ImmediateResponse` message has been changed from `string` to `bytes`.\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;  // <-- was string\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;  // <-- changed to bytes\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**Why This Changed:**\nChanging to `bytes` allows more flexible handling of binary content and is more idiomatic for protobuf. The `string` type in protobuf enforces UTF-8 validation, which can be restrictive for response bodies that may contain binary data or non-UTF-8 encoded content.\n\n**Migration Action Required:**\n- **For Go clients:** Code must change from `response.GetBody()` (returns `string`) to `response.GetBody()` (returns `[]byte`). Generated code will handle this automatically with regenerated protobuf files.\n- **For Python clients:** Code using `response.body` will now return `bytes` instead of `str`. String responses should be encoded: `response.body = your_string.encode('utf-8')`\n- **For other languages:** Regenerate protobuf code and update type conversions accordingly.\n\n**Example:**\n\nGo (before):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   \"Hello World\",  // string\n}\n```\n\nGo (after):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Hello World\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. disable_clear_route_cache Field (Deprecated with Replacement)\n\n**Deprecation Status:** Marked for future removal (recommended to migrate)\n\n**What's Happening:**\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is being superseded by a new `route_cache_action` enum that provides more granular control over route cache behavior.\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ... other fields ...\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // Default: clear route cache when external processor response sets\n    // clear_route_cache = true\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear route cache regardless of clear_route_cache field\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Never clear route cache regardless of clear_route_cache field\n    // (equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache = true)\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  // ... other fields ...\n\n  // Deprecated: use route_cache_action instead\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Recommended: new field for route cache control\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Recommendation:**\n\n| Old Configuration | New Configuration | Behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Default behavior - respect external processor's clear_route_cache field |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear route cache |\n| Not set | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | (New) Always clear route cache |\n\n**Example:**\n\nYAML (before - v1.30):\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nYAML (after - v1.31, recommended):\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Replaces disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**What It Is:**\nA new enum-based configuration that replaces the boolean `disable_clear_route_cache` flag with more explicit control over route cache behavior in response to external processor requests.\n\n**Field Details:**\n- **Field Number:** 18\n- **Type:** `enum RouteCacheAction`\n- **Location:** `ExternalProcessor` message in `ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Values:**\n\n| Value | Name | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| 0 | DEFAULT | Clear route cache only when the external processor response sets `clear_route_cache = true`. This is the default behavior and maintains backward compatibility. |\n| 1 | CLEAR | Always clear the route cache when processing request headers, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the external processor response. Use this when headers are frequently modified in ways that affect routing. |\n| 2 | RETAIN | Never clear the route cache, even if the external processor response sets `clear_route_cache = true`. Use this when you're confident that header modifications won't affect routing, to improve performance. |\n\n**When to Use Each:**\n\n- **DEFAULT:** Most common use case. Allows the external processor to indicate when the route needs to be recomputed based on header modifications.\n- **CLEAR:** When the external processor frequently modifies routing-critical headers (e.g., authority, path) and you want to ensure the route is always recomputed for safety.\n- **RETAIN:** Performance optimization when headers are modified but routing is known to be unaffected (e.g., only adding custom headers).\n\n**Implementation Note:**\nThe configuration is only applied to request headers processing. The field is ignored for body and trailer responses.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Management\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**What It Is:**\nEnhanced support for observability mode with deferred stream closure management. Previously, gRPC streams would be immediately closed in observability mode. Now they can be held open longer to ensure all data is delivered.\n\n**New Fields:**\n\n**Field: deferred_close_timeout**\n- **Field Number:** 19\n- **Type:** `google.protobuf.Duration`\n- **Default:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n- **Description:** Specifies how long to keep gRPC streams open after the HTTP request/response lifecycle completes when running in observability mode.\n\n**Configuration Example:**\n\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Wait 10 seconds before closing streams\n```\n\n**How It Works:**\n\nIn observability mode:\n1. Envoy sends requests to the external processor without expecting responses\n2. The external processor cannot modify the request/response\n3. With `deferred_close_timeout`, the stream stays open for the specified duration after the HTTP stream ends\n4. This ensures all observability data reaches the external processor reliably\n5. After the timeout, the stream is automatically closed\n\n**Typical Use Cases:**\n- Monitoring and logging services that need to observe all traffic\n- Analytics collection that doesn't require low-latency responses\n- Security monitoring and intrusion detection systems\n\n---\n\n### 3. Enhanced Implementation Infrastructure\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**Behind-the-Scenes Changes:**\n\nTwo new internal classes were added to support deferred stream closure:\n\n1. **ThreadLocalStreamManager:** Manages the lifecycle of gRPC streams with deferred closure support\n   - Stores streams in a thread-local map by stream ID\n   - Handles deferred erasure (closure) of streams\n   - Ensures stream cleanup happens on the correct thread\n\n2. **DeferredDeletableStream:** Wraps a gRPC stream with deferred closure capability\n   - Sets up a timer for deferred closure\n   - Tracks stream lifecycle until the timer fires\n   - Manages resources properly across thread boundaries\n\n**Impact:** These are internal implementation details. Users don't need to interact with them directly, but they enable the observability mode enhancements described above.\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Summary of Configuration Changes\n\n| Aspect | v1.30 | v1.31 | Migration Path |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Route Cache Control | `disable_clear_route_cache` (bool) | `route_cache_action` (enum) + deprecated bool | Migrate to enum |\n| Deferred Close | Not supported | `deferred_close_timeout` | Add if using observability mode |\n| Immediate Response Body | `string` | `bytes` | Update client code |\n| Stream Lifecycle | Immediate close | Deferred close (configurable) | Configure as needed |\n\n### Full Configuration Template (v1.31)\n\n```yaml\n# HTTP Connection Manager configuration\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n\n    # Required: gRPC service configuration\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      timeout: 5s\n\n    # Optional: failure handling\n    failure_mode_allow: false\n\n    # Optional: processing mode (what to send to external processor)\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: NONE\n      response_body_mode: NONE\n      request_trailer_mode: SKIP\n      response_trailer_mode: SKIP\n\n    # Optional: message timeout\n    message_timeout: 200ms\n    max_message_timeout: 10s\n\n    # Optional: statistics prefix\n    stat_prefix: my_ext_proc\n\n    # Optional: header mutation rules\n    mutation_rules:\n      allow_all_routing:\n        value: true\n      allow_envoy:\n        value: true\n\n    # NEW in v1.31: route cache control\n    # RECOMMENDED: use route_cache_action instead of disable_clear_route_cache\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # or CLEAR, or RETAIN\n\n    # DEPRECATED in v1.31: use route_cache_action instead\n    # disable_clear_route_cache: false\n\n    # Optional: allow mode override\n    allow_mode_override: true\n\n    # Optional: disable immediate response\n    disable_immediate_response: false\n\n    # Optional: header forwarding rules\n    forward_rules:\n      allowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - exact: \"custom-header\"\n      disallowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - prefix: \"secret-\"\n\n    # Optional: dynamic metadata options\n    metadata_options:\n      forwarding_namespaces:\n        untyped:\n        - my_namespace\n      receiving_namespaces:\n        untyped:\n        - response_namespace\n\n    # Optional: observability mode\n    observability_mode: true\n\n    # NEW in v1.31: deferred close timeout for observability mode\n    deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Default is 5000ms\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Handling\n\n**Default Behavior Change (Minor):**\n\nIn v1.30, `disable_clear_route_cache` defaulted to `false`, which meant:\n- Clear route cache when external processor sets `clear_route_cache = true`\n- Keep route cache otherwise\n\nIn v1.31, `route_cache_action` defaults to `DEFAULT`, which has the same behavior:\n- Clear route cache when external processor sets `clear_route_cache = true`\n- Keep route cache otherwise\n\n**Impact:** If you're using the defaults, there's no behavior change.\n\n**If you had `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n- Old behavior: Never clear route cache\n- New equivalent: `route_cache_action: RETAIN` (same behavior)\n- Recommendation: Update configuration to use the new enum\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Handling\n\n**New Behavior:**\n\nStreams in observability mode are now managed with deferred closure:\n\n1. Stream stays open for `deferred_close_timeout` after HTTP stream completes\n2. Allows all pending observability messages to reach the external processor\n3. Stream is then automatically closed\n\n**Old Behavior (v1.30):**\nStreams were closed as soon as the HTTP request/response processing completed.\n\n**Impact:**\n\n- **Improved Reliability:** Observability data is less likely to be lost\n- **Slight Resource Usage:** Streams hold resources for up to 5 seconds (default) after completion\n- **Configurable:** Adjust `deferred_close_timeout` based on your external processor's processing speed\n\n**Example Scenario:**\n\nExternal processor doing log aggregation in observability mode:\n- Request completes in 100ms\n- Stream would close immediately (v1.30) or after 5s (v1.31, default)\n- Asyncronous logging operations in the external processor have more time to complete\n- Logs are more likely to be captured and forwarded before stream closure\n\n### 3. Immediate Response Format Compatibility\n\n**Technical Impact:**\n\nThe `body` field type change from `string` to `bytes` in `ImmediateResponse` requires regenerating protobuf files in external processors.\n\n**Runtime Behavior:**\n- If the external processor doesn't send body content, no changes needed\n- If body content is sent as UTF-8 text, automatic encoding/decoding handles it\n- If body content contains binary data, the new `bytes` type is actually more appropriate\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n\nReview your ext_proc filter configurations to identify:\n\n1. **Do you use `disable_clear_route_cache`?**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/config\n   ```\n   - If yes, go to Step 2\n   - If no, skip to Step 3\n\n2. **Do you use observability mode?**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"observability_mode.*true\" /path/to/config\n   ```\n   - If yes, go to Step 3\n   - If no, skip to Step 4\n\n### Step 2: Migrate disable_clear_route_cache\n\nUpdate each configuration that uses `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**Find:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Replace with:**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Or find:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: false\n# or not set (defaults to false)\n```\n\n**Replace with:**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n### Step 3: Configure Deferred Close Timeout (Optional)\n\nIf using observability mode, consider adding explicit configuration:\n\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Adjust based on your external processor\n```\n\nThe default is 5 seconds. Adjust based on:\n- How fast your external processor can process messages\n- How much resource overhead you can tolerate\n- How critical it is to deliver all observability data\n\n**Recommendations:**\n- **1-2 seconds:** For high-throughput scenarios with fast processors\n- **5 seconds (default):** Balanced approach for most use cases\n- **10+ seconds:** For slow processors or when observability is critical\n\n### Step 4: Update External Processor Code\n\nIf your external processor sends `ImmediateResponse` messages:\n\n**Python Example:**\n\nBefore (v1.30):\n```python\nfrom envoy.service.ext_proc.v3 import external_processor_pb2\n\nresponse = external_processor_pb2.ImmediateResponse()\nresponse.status.code = 200\nresponse.body = \"Hello World\"  # string\n```\n\nAfter (v1.31):\n```python\nfrom envoy.service.ext_proc.v3 import external_processor_pb2\n\nresponse = external_processor_pb2.ImmediateResponse()\nresponse.status.code = 200\nresponse.body = b\"Hello World\"  # bytes\n```\n\n**Go Example:**\n\nBefore (v1.30):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   \"Hello World\",  // string\n}\n```\n\nAfter (v1.31):\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Hello World\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n**Regenerate Protobuf Bindings:**\n\nAll language bindings need to be regenerated with the updated protobuf definitions:\n\n```bash\n# Go\nprotoc --go_out=. envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto\n\n# Python\npython -m grpc_tools.protoc ...\n\n# Node.js\ngrpc_tools_node_protoc ...\n\n# See language-specific documentation for exact commands\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test and Validate\n\n#### Configuration Validation\n\n```bash\n# Check syntax\nenvoy -c your-config.yaml --mode validate_only\n\n# Verify ext_proc filter is loaded\nenvoy -c your-config.yaml --mode dump_config | grep ext_proc\n```\n\n#### Functional Testing\n\n1. **Test with observability mode disabled:**\n   - Verify normal request processing works\n   - Confirm route cache behavior matches expectations\n   - Check metrics and logs\n\n2. **Test with observability mode enabled:**\n   - Send traffic through the filter\n   - Verify all observability messages reach the external processor\n   - Monitor for lost data with and without `deferred_close_timeout`\n   - Check CPU and memory impact\n\n3. **Test ImmediateResponse (if applicable):**\n   - Send immediate responses from external processor\n   - Verify body content is correctly delivered to client\n   - Test with binary response data if applicable\n\n#### Metrics to Monitor\n\n```\n# Route cache metrics\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.clear_route_cache_ignored\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.clear_route_cache_disabled\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.clear_route_cache_upstream_ignored\n\n# Stream metrics\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.streams_started\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.streams_closed\nhttp.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.streams_failed\n```\n\n### Step 6: Canary Deployment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy binary to a canary environment\n2. Route 5-10% of traffic to canary instances\n3. Monitor for 24-48 hours:\n   - Error rates\n   - Latency percentiles\n   - External processor CPU/memory usage\n   - Observability data completeness\n4. If issues arise, adjust `deferred_close_timeout` or `route_cache_action` settings\n5. Gradually increase traffic percentage\n6. Full production rollout\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Unit Test Updates\n\nFor external processor implementations, update unit tests:\n\n**Python:**\n```python\ndef test_immediate_response_body():\n    # v1.31 requires bytes, not string\n    response = external_processor_pb2.ImmediateResponse()\n    response.body = b\"test content\"\n    assert isinstance(response.body, bytes)\n    assert response.body == b\"test content\"\n```\n\n**Go:**\n```go\nfunc TestImmediateResponseBody(t *testing.T) {\n    resp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n        Status: &type_v3.HttpStatus{Code: 200},\n        Body:   []byte(\"test content\"),\n    }\n    assert.Equal(t, []byte(\"test content\"), resp.GetBody())\n}\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n1. **Route Cache Control:**\n   - Test with `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` - verify external processor can trigger cache clear\n   - Test with `route_cache_action: CLEAR` - verify cache always clears\n   - Test with `route_cache_action: RETAIN` - verify cache never clears\n\n2. **Observability Mode:**\n   - Enable observability mode with various `deferred_close_timeout` values\n   - Send requests that modify headers\n   - Verify all observability messages reach the external processor\n   - Measure stream lifecycle and resource usage\n\n3. **Immediate Response:**\n   - Send immediate responses with text body\n   - Send immediate responses with binary body\n   - Verify content reaches client correctly\n\n### Performance Testing\n\n```bash\n# Load test with observability mode on/off\n# Monitor:\n# - CPU usage\n# - Memory usage\n# - Stream open/close rates\n# - Lost observability messages\n# - Latency impact\n\nwrk -t 4 -c 100 -d 60s \\\n    -s /path/to/script.lua \\\n    http://envoy:8080/test_path\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Issues Occur After Upgrade\n\n1. **Immediate Action:**\n   ```bash\n   # Roll back to v1.30\n   systemctl stop envoy\n   cp /path/to/envoy-v1.30 /usr/local/bin/envoy\n   systemctl start envoy\n   ```\n\n2. **Before Next Upgrade Attempt:**\n   - Identify the problematic feature (route cache, observability, immediate response)\n   - Disable or adjust that feature\n   - Run targeted tests\n   - Attempt upgrade again\n\n3. **Common Rollback Scenarios:**\n\n   **Scenario: External processor crashes on receiving ImmediateResponse**\n   - Cause: Protobuf mismatch on body field (bytes vs string)\n   - Solution: Regenerate protobuf bindings in external processor\n   - Prevention: Test with external processor built against v1.31 protobuf definitions\n\n   **Scenario: Route cache behavior changed unexpectedly**\n   - Cause: Didn't update `disable_clear_route_cache` to new enum\n   - Solution: Explicitly set `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (same as old default)\n   - Prevention: Review configuration and test route behavior\n\n   **Scenario: High resource usage with observability mode**\n   - Cause: Default 5-second deferred close timeout too long for your workload\n   - Solution: Reduce `deferred_close_timeout` to 1-2 seconds\n   - Prevention: Test and tune timeout value before full rollout\n\n---\n\n## Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Mixing Old and New Configuration Styles\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting settings!\n```\n\n**Solution:** Use only `route_cache_action`. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache`.\n\n### Pitfall 2: Not Regenerating Protobuf Code\n\n**Problem:** External processor fails when receiving `ImmediateResponse` from v1.31 Envoy.\n\n**Cause:** Old protobuf code expects `body` to be string, but v1.31 Envoy sends bytes.\n\n**Solution:**\n```bash\n# Regenerate all protobuf bindings\npython -m grpc_tools.protoc \\\n    --python_out=. \\\n    --grpc_python_out=. \\\n    -I/path/to/envoy/api \\\n    -I/path/to/googleapis \\\n    envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Observability Data Loss with Short Timeout\n\n**Problem:** In observability mode with short `deferred_close_timeout`, async logging operations in external processor don't complete before stream closes.\n\n**Solution:** Increase `deferred_close_timeout` based on external processor's typical processing time:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Increase from default 5s\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Not Testing Route Cache Behavior\n\n**Problem:** After upgrade, routing behavior changes unexpectedly.\n\n**Cause:** Didn't explicitly set `route_cache_action`, relying on undefined default behavior.\n\n**Solution:** Always explicitly set the value:\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Be explicit about intended behavior\n```\n\n### Pitfall 5: Canary Test with Old External Processor Version\n\n**Problem:** Canary deployment with v1.31 Envoy but v1.30 external processor fails.\n\n**Cause:** ImmediateResponse body format mismatch.\n\n**Solution:** Upgrade external processor to v1.31 compatible version first, or thoroughly test compatibility.\n\n---\n\n## Backwards Compatibility Notes\n\n### What's Backwards Compatible\n\n- ✅ Normal request/response processing\n- ✅ Default configurations (will work with v1.30 external processors)\n- ✅ Processing modes and timeout configuration\n- ✅ Header mutation rules\n\n### What Requires Updates\n\n- ❌ `ImmediateResponse.body` field (type change: string → bytes)\n- ❌ `disable_clear_route_cache` (replacement with `route_cache_action` enum)\n- ❌ Observability mode with deferred closure (v1.31 feature)\n\n### Migration Strategy for Large Deployments\n\n1. **Phase 1:** Deploy v1.31 Envoy with all old configurations (will work)\n2. **Phase 2:** Update external processor code to handle bytes body\n3. **Phase 3:** Update Envoy configurations to use new enums\n4. **Phase 4:** Optimize observability mode settings\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Official Documentation\n\n- [Envoy External Processing Filter Documentation](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter)\n- [ext_proc Proto API Reference](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/api-v3/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto)\n- [External Processor Service Proto](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/api-v3/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto)\n\n### Release Notes\n\n- [Envoy v1.31.0 Release Notes](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/version_history)\n\n### Community Support\n\n- [Envoy GitHub Issues](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues)\n- [Envoy Discussion Forum](https://discuss.envoyproxy.io/)\n- [Slack Community](https://envoyproxy.slack.com/)\n\n---\n\n## Checklist for Successful Migration\n\n- [ ] Review current ext_proc configurations\n- [ ] Identify use of `disable_clear_route_cache` or observability mode\n- [ ] Regenerate protobuf bindings for external processor\n- [ ] Update external processor code for `ImmediateResponse.body` (bytes)\n- [ ] Update Envoy configurations to use `route_cache_action` enum\n- [ ] Configure `deferred_close_timeout` if using observability mode\n- [ ] Test in non-production environment\n- [ ] validate_only`\n4. **Contact Envoy community** via GitHub issues or discussion forums\n5. **Work with vendor support** if using Envoy through a distribution\n\n---\n\n**Document Version:**
